ch 9

The lore has been updated: Sariel and her brothers have not been born yet. Alexiel is a young woman of sixteen, and her relationship with Artorius is brand new. This makes her journey to the capital a true foray into the unknown, without the complication of a family she has yet to build.

Here is the scene detailing her arrival in Aeterna.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 10. Afternoon.]

[Location: The God-Road, approaching Aeterna.]

For weeks, they had traveled east, a small, silent procession moving at a relentless pace. The journey had been a blur of perfectly maintained roads, orderly towns, and the unnerving, silent presence of Raziel and his Guard. Alexiel had been treated not as a prisoner, but as a specimen—given clean quarters, good food, and absolutely no freedom or conversation.

Then, they crested a high ridge, and she saw it.

Aeterna. The heart of the Celestial Imperium.

It was not a city; it was a statement. An impossibly vast ring of gleaming white marble walls rose from the plains, so high that clouds drifted past their mid-point. Inside, elegant towers and domes of silver and gold stretched towards the sky. And at its very center, a single, needle-thin spire of a shining, otherworldly material pierced the heavens—the Zenith Spire, the Empyrean Citadel, the seat of the absent Creator.

Alexiel’s first thought was purely tactical. It's indefensible. The grandeur was a weakness. The sprawling, open avenues were perfect for an invading army. The ornamental towers were strategically worthless. She saw a thousand ways to bring it to its knees.

Her second thought was one of suffocating awe. This was the order her "father" Lucifer raged against. It was ancient, magnificent, and eternal. It was the legacy of the beings whose blood ran, however flawed, in her own veins.

As they rode through the colossal main gate, the sounds of the city washed over her. It was a low, orderly hum—the murmur of a million voices, the distant ring of a craftsman's hammer, the rumble of carts on stone. There was no chaos, no shouting, no drunken brawls like in the camps of the Host. The people who lined the grand boulevards were well-fed, their clothes clean. But their faces were impassive, their eyes incurious. They stared at the Silent Guard with a familiar, fearful deference. They stared at Alexiel, at her Unseeing Eyes, with a mixture of hatred and fascination.

They did not ride to a fortress or a barracks. Raziel led them directly down the grand processional way, toward the impossible needle of the Zenith Spire. As they passed into its immense shadow, the Lord Regent glided his horse closer to hers.

"Welcome home, child of the Empyrean," Raziel whispered, his voice dripping with an ancient, chilling irony.

Alexiel looked up at the Spire that seemed to hold up the sky, feeling like a fly entering a spider's web. She was no longer a soldier on a battlefield she understood. She was now a piece in a game she had yet to learn, played by a master who had been moving pieces since before her world had a history.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 10. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: The Chamber of Stilled Stars, Empyrean Citadel, Aeterna.]

The chamber was a perfect sphere of seamless, night-black stone. There were no windows, no doors, no torches. The only light came from a single, unmoving point of white fire that hung in the exact center of the room, casting no shadows. The air was cold, ancient, and utterly still. This was Raziel’s sanctum, a place outside of time.

He sat on a simple stone bench. Alexiel stood before him, the two Silent Guard who had escorted her having vanished the moment the door sealed.

"Sit," Raziel whispered. Another bench, identical to his own, rose silently from the floor opposite him.

Alexiel obeyed, her movements calm and deliberate. She would show no fear.

Raziel studied her for a long time, his Unseeing Eyes seeming to peer into her very soul. When he finally spoke, his question was not about armies or strategies. It was a surgeon's probe, aimed at the heart of her identity.

"Your eyes," he said, his voice a dry rustle. "The mark of the Null. A flaw in an otherwise perfect design. Does it anger you?"

Alexiel met his gaze. This was the opening move. She had to answer as the Reluctant Champion, not the calculating mind. "It is my truth, Lord Regent," she replied, her voice quiet. "I cannot be angered by what I am. I have simply learned to make a strength of my limitations."

"A noble sentiment," Raziel murmured, though his tone held no warmth. "Lucifer also believed in making a strength of what others saw as flaws. He taught you his philosophy. He molded you in his image. Why did you, his perfect tool, decide your creator's design was flawed?"

She had prepared for this. She let the genuine horror of Silverwood rise within her, using the real trauma to fuel her performance. "A design that requires the murder of children is not perfection, Lord Regent. It is a monstrous calculation. I chose to be a flawed person rather than a perfect monster."

"Monstrosity is a judgment made by the sentimental," Raziel countered, his voice a sliver of ice. "To the universe, there is only function. An action is either efficient, or it is not. Lucifer's methods at Silverwood were tactically inefficient. Was that not your true, dispassionate conclusion?"

He was testing her, trying to see if she was a fellow pragmatist hiding behind a convenient moral shield. She had to reject his inexorable reasoning completely.

"The death of a child can never be efficient, Lord Regent," she said, her voice firm with a conviction she knew Artorius would have admired. "It creates a debt that can never be repaid. That is a truth that exists beyond any calculation."

Her answer was flawless. An emotional, moral absolute that his own system could not easily parse. He fell silent again, observing her. He could not find a crack in her armor.

"A compelling philosophy," he said finally. "Let us see how deep it runs."

He leaned forward slightly. "There is a cancer within the Imperium. A faction of sentimentalists who believe in a history that is not our own. They trade in forbidden texts and whisper that our bloodline is a lie. They call themselves the Revisionist Scholars."

He watched her face for any flicker of recognition, any sign of deceit. "You claim you wish to serve a just and orderly Imperium. Such an order cannot abide a cancer. You are a weapon that has proven effective at... purging. Help me locate the heart of this heresy. Help me cut it out. Prove your loyalty."

The test had been laid bare. It was not a request; it was a command. He was ordering her to hunt down and destroy the very people she might see as fellow truth-seekers, forcing her to choose between her mask of loyalty and her own hidden agenda.

You're right. That's a fair criticism. The previous version was too theatrical. A more subtle and grounded approach would be more effective and chilling, making the crack in her facade more unsettling.

Let's revise that scene.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Dead of Night.]

[Location: Alexiel's Suite, Zenith Spire, Aeterna.]

Sleep offered no escape, only a different kind of battlefield. Alexiel was back in the chaos of the waterfall cave, her mind replaying the fight in a series of sharp, violent flashes: the clang of steel, the weight of a parry, the grunt of a dying Host warrior. It wasn't a nightmare of fear, but a disorienting, feverish dream of pure, kinetic violence, a chaotic mix of adrenaline and horror.

She awoke with a silent gasp, her body tensed, her hand instinctively reaching for a sword that wasn't there. Her heart hammered against her ribs, her senses on high alert, scanning the unfamiliar shadows of the suite for threats.

A soft knock came at her door.

Before she could fully suppress her combat instincts, the door opened a crack. It was Artorius. He held a small, leather-bound book in his hand. "Alexiel? I saw your light was still on. I was worried you couldn't sleep. I thought perhaps..."

His voice trailed off as he saw her. For a split second, he didn't see the broken soldier or the grieving defector he had come to know. He saw the woman from the battlements. She was sitting upright in bed, her back perfectly straight, her Unseeing Eyes wide and intensely focused, staring not at him, but at the shadows in the corner of the room. There was no fear or sadness in her expression; there was only the absolute, chilling stillness of a predator scanning for threats. It was a look of pure, dispassionate competence that was more unsettling than any open hostility.

She blinked, and the look vanished as if it had never been. The impenetrable warrior was gone, replaced once more by the weary woman. The tension left her shoulders, and she seemed to shrink slightly, pulling a blanket around herself.

"A nightmare?" Artorius asked softly, his concern genuine.

Alexiel took a moment to compose herself, her breathing still a little too sharp. She nodded slowly, looking down at her hands. "Just... a memory," she said, her voice rough. "From the field. It is difficult to leave the battlefield behind."

Her explanation was simple, understated, and utterly believable. Artorius's concern deepened with sympathy. He hadn't seen a monster. He had seen the look of a true, battle-hardened veteran, a haunted gaze he had only ever witnessed in the most elite soldiers after a horrific campaign. He had not seen her true nature, only what he perceived as its terrible cost. His desire to protect her from her own memories intensified.

He stepped forward and placed the book on her nightstand. "Forgive me," he said softly. "I should not have disturbed you. Try to rest, Alexiel. You are safe here."

He closed the door, leaving her alone once more. Alexiel's composure held until she heard his footsteps fade down the hall. Only then did she allow herself a single, shuddering breath. She had not been afraid of the nightmare. She had been terrified that, for a moment, Artorius had seen how much she had enjoyed it.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Morning.]

[Location: A Private Training Terrace, Zenith Spire, Aeterna.]

The next morning, Artorius found Alexiel in her suite, staring out the crystal window, the very picture of weary grace. When she turned to greet him, she seemed composed, but he could see a shadow of the previous night's hauntedness lingering in her eyes.

"Idleness is a poison to a soldier's mind," he said without preamble. "I have arranged something. Please, come with me."

He led her not into the political heart of the Citadel, but up a series of winding stairs to a place of quiet solitude: a private training terrace, open to the sky. The floor was white marble, polished to a mirror shine. A single, ancient ironwood tree with silver leaves grew in a planter in the center, and the terrace overlooked the breathtaking panorama of the city below.

On a simple wooden rack rested a collection of blunted, perfectly balanced practice swords.

"I know my father's mission weighs on you," Artorius said gently, his voice full of a sincerity that still unsettled her. "And after last night... I thought perhaps holding a blade again, not in anger, but in practice, might help quiet the memories. No one will watch. No one will judge. This is just for you."

His offer was deeply thoughtful, a gesture that spoke to the warrior she was, not the political piece she had become. She feigned a moment of hesitation, then gave him a small, grateful nod.

She selected a simple longsword, its weight familiar in her hand. Artorius picked up another. "Just to move," he offered. "To find your center."

They began to spar. Artorius was a son of the Imperium, his technique powerful, precise, and honorable. He was an excellent swordsman.

He was not prepared for Alexiel.

She moved with an impossible, liquid grace. She held back her true strength, her secret magic, her killing intent—she held back everything that made her a predator—and yet, she was still a force beyond his comprehension. Her parries were not just blocks; they were effortless redirections of his momentum that left him subtly off-balance. Her footwork was so perfect she seemed to be exactly where his blade wasn't, a moment before he even decided to strike.

It was not a duel. It was a lesson. She never once went on the offensive, yet he felt utterly defeated, his every move anticipated and neutralized with a chilling, beautiful efficiency.

Finally, he lowered his sword, breathless and sweating, a look of pure astonishment on his face. "The stories," he panted, a disbelieving laugh escaping him. "They don't do you justice. They don't even come close."

They stood in the center of the terrace, close enough that he could see the faint, porcelain fractures in her Unseeing Eyes. For a moment, the air was charged with a new kind of tension—not of combat, but of a shared, intense respect.

Alexiel lowered her own blade, allowing a look of calm relief to grace her features. "You were right, my Prince," she said, her voice soft and genuine, for this one small thing was true. "It... helped. Thank you."

Artorius looked at this incredible woman—a warrior of impossible skill, yet haunted by a trauma so deep he could only guess at its edges. His resolve to protect her, to be her shield against his father and her own past, hardened into an unshakeable conviction. He had no idea that the predator he was trying to heal was merely enjoying the chance to stretch her claws.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Afternoon.]

[Location: The Great Archives, Zenith Spire, Aeterna.]

The Great Archives of Aeterna were less a library and more a tomb of knowledge. Shelves carved from the black stone of the Spire itself stretched up into a gloom that no torch could fully penetrate. The air was cold, still, and thick with the scent of ancient paper, drying ink, and a profound, oppressive silence.

Prince Artorius led Alexiel through the towering aisles, his footsteps echoing in the vast chamber. "If there is a seditious academic movement in this city," he whispered, his voice full of conviction, "its heart will be here. Knowledge is their weapon."

Alexiel nodded, her Unseeing Eyes taking in everything. And its greatest weakness, she thought. The records of their heresy must exist somewhere within the system meant to condemn it.

They approached the central scriptorium, a wide, ink-stained desk where a frail, elderly man sat hunched over a massive, open tome. His fingers were stained black to the knuckles, and he peered at the text through lenses thick enough to distort his sharp, intelligent eyes. This was Magister Lucian Kantos, the Keeper of the Hallowed Archives, a man who had served the Imperium for two centuries.

He looked up as they approached, his expression one of fussy annoyance, which quickly morphed into shocked deference as he recognized the Prince. He rose slowly, bowing with a creak of old bones.

"My Prince," he rasped. "An unexpected honor."

"Magister Kantos," Artorius said with formal courtesy. "The Lord Regent has tasked us with a delicate matter. We are investigating a potential cell of... seditious scholars. We require access to the withdrawal logs for all texts pertaining to the Age of Rebellion and the Great Vanishing for the past five years."

Lucian’s eyes widened behind his lenses. Alexiel watched him, her senses on high alert. She saw the flicker of terror, but it was immediately masked by a performance of loyal indignation.

"Sedition? In my archives?" he sputtered. "A terrible business. Of course, my Prince. I will assist in any way I can. Such heresy must be rooted out."

While Artorius began discussing specific search parameters with the Magister, Alexiel observed. Lucian was a perfect Imperial servant. But his fear felt… specific. His hands trembled just a little too much. He agreed a little too quickly. Her mind, honed by Lucifer's lessons in spotting deception, tagged him as a person of interest.

She waited for a pause in their conversation before interjecting, her voice quiet and academic to match her surroundings. "Magister," she began, "while serving the Host, I encountered a field report that mentioned an obscure text being sought by Imperial agents. It was called The Vanishing: A Metaphysical Refutation. Are you familiar with it?"

It was a complete fabrication. A lure.

Lucian Kantos froze for a fraction of a second. It was an almost imperceptible pause, but to Alexiel, it was a deafening confession. His eyes darted to hers, then away.

"I... I can't say that I am, my Lady," he stammered, turning to his own records. "The title is not familiar. So many heretical texts were produced in that chaotic era. I will search the forbidden registry for you."

Artorius nodded, satisfied. But Alexiel now knew with absolute conviction. Magister Kantos was not just a loyal servant. He was her first real lead. He was either a member of the Revisionist Scholars, or he knew who they were. The hunter had found her prey.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: A private study carrel, The Great Archives, Aeterna.]

The hours bled into one another in the silent, dusty air of the Great Archives. They sat at a heavy oak table, surrounded by towering stacks of withdrawal ledgers, each one a monument to forgotten knowledge. Artorius worked with the diligent focus of a true scholar, his brow furrowed as he cross-referenced names and dates, hunting for a pattern.

Alexiel worked with a different kind of focus. She was not just searching; she was constructing.

She let out a soft, thoughtful hum, just loud enough to break his concentration. "That's... odd," she murmured, tapping a finger on an open ledger.

Artorius looked up. "What is it?"

"This withdrawal record," she said, pushing the heavy book towards him. "For a copy of 'The Reign of the Apostates.' The authorization signature is Magister Kantos's, which is standard. But the return signature... it is smudged beyond recognition. And the date logged for its return is a day before it was checked out." She shrugged, a perfect picture of mild confusion. "A simple clerical error, I suppose."

Artorius frowned at the entry, making a note of the inconsistency. They returned to their work. Twenty minutes later, Alexiel spoke again, her voice still quiet.

"My Prince... look at this. A request for access to the sealed section on pre-Imperial history. Again, authorized by the Magister, as is required. But the requestor's name is listed as Lord Erevan of House Tyrell."

"I am not familiar with that house," Artorius said.

"Neither is the Imperial Registry," Alexiel replied softly. "They went extinct during the Thousand Year War. A ghost has been reading in the archives."

She continued this pattern for the next hour, "discovering" three more small, seemingly unrelated anomalies. A duplicate request for a single controversial text, both authorized by Kantos on the same day. A security log detailing a magical ward fizzling out for ten minutes on a specific floor, with the only person present being the Magister himself. She never once mentioned his name with suspicion, only as the one common factor in a series of confusing puzzles.

Artorius grew frustrated. "The standards in this place have fallen," he muttered, running a hand through his hair. "Sloppy records, ghost signatures... how can we possibly find a conspiracy in all this noise?"

Alexiel remained silent, watching him. She had laid out the pieces. Now she would see if the noble prince was also a detective.

He stared at the five ledgers she had pushed to the center of the table, his eyes tracing the connections. The smudged return. The ghost's request. The duplicate entry. The fizzled ward. His frustration slowly subsided, replaced by a dawning, cold suspicion.

"No," he said slowly, his eyes widening as he looked up at her. "This isn't noise. It's the opposite. It's a deliberate smokescreen." He pointed to each anomaly. "The only constant in every single one of these 'errors'... is Magister Kantos's authorization."

His voice dropped to a grim whisper. "This isn't sloppiness. This is deliberate. He's hiding something by creating false trails in his own archives."

Alexiel allowed a look of shocked realization to cross her face. She had played her part perfectly. "The Keeper of the Archives himself?" she asked, her voice filled with feigned disbelief. "But why would he do such a thing?"

Artorius looked at the evidence, his expression now hard with purpose. He had taken the bait she had so carefully laid. The investigation was now focused exactly where she wanted it to be.

"I don't know," he said. "But we are going to find out."

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: Magister Lucian Kantos's office, The Great Archives, Aeterna.]

"He is hiding something," Artorius said, his voice a low growl of frustrated conviction. "And by the Creator, I will have the truth of it."

Alexiel, internally, assessed the Prince's decision. A direct confrontation was clumsy, a brute-force approach to a problem that required a scalpel. But it was also decisive. It would force their opponent's hand. She gave a slow, supportive nod. "As you command, my Prince."

They didn't wait. Artorius gathered the five suspect ledgers, his expression grim, and led the way back through the silent archives to the Magister's private office. He did not knock.

Lucian Kantos looked up from a delicate scroll, his eyes widening in surprise and then dawning fear as the Prince strode into his office, Alexiel a silent shadow at his back.

Artorius dropped the heavy ledgers onto the Magister's pristine desk with a resounding thump that made the old man jump.

"Magister Kantos," Artorius began, his voice devoid of its earlier warmth. "We have found numerous discrepancies in your logs. False entries. Impossible timelines. Authorizations for houses that have been dust for two hundred years. All under your personal seal." He leaned forward, his hands flat on the desk. "Explain yourself."

Lucian’s face went pale. He began to stammer, playing the part of a confused, overwhelmed bureaucrat. "My Prince! An error! It must be! The archives are so vast, my staff so small... I am an old man, oversights are..."

"These are not oversights," Artorius cut him off, his voice like iron. "They are lies. A deliberate and systematic effort to obscure the truth. Are you protecting someone, old man? Are you the heart of this heresy my father sent me to find?"

The old scholar began to tremble, his eyes darting between the Prince's righteous fury and Alexiel's silent, unnerving stare. It was Alexiel who spoke next, her voice quiet but carrying a deadly precision.

"Your memory seemed flawless when we discussed the complex genealogy of House Tyrell just an hour ago, Magister," she observed.

The simple, factual statement cut through Lucian's defense like a razor. His facade crumbled. He looked from one to the other, his eyes filled with the terror of a trapped animal. He saw no escape.

With a sudden, desperate cry, he lunged across his desk, not for a weapon, but for a single, leather-bound book sitting on a pedestal. "You don't understand!" he shrieked, grabbing it. "It must be protected!"

He turned and threw the book towards the roaring fireplace at the far end of the office.

Artorius shouted in alarm, but Alexiel moved with the speed of a predator. She launched herself forward, not at Lucian, but at the book. She caught it in mid-air, just inches from the flames, tumbling into a graceful roll on the carpet and rising to her feet, the book clutched tightly in her hands.

She stood, holding the book, and looked at the trembling, defeated old man. Artorius, his sword now drawn, had Lucian cornered against the wall.

The investigation had just become a confession. They had their heretic.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: Magister Lucian Kantos's office, The Great Archives, Aeterna.]

Artorius unbound the old man's hands himself, a gesture of respect that seemed to surprise Lucian Kantos more than the threat of a sword. The Prince pushed a goblet of water across the desk. Alexiel stood silently by the hearth, holding the coded book, her presence a cold, watchful weight in the room.

"Magister," Artorius began, his tone quiet and earnest. "I do not believe you are a simple traitor. I believe you are a man who sought a truth you felt was denied. My father sees only heresy, but I see a question that deserves an answer. Help me understand."

Kantos looked from the Prince's open, sincere face to Alexiel's unreadable mask and back again. He was a cornered animal, unsure which predator to fear more. "Understand?" he rasped, his voice thin. "My Prince, your father would have my head for the books I've read. What I have done... he would unmake my very soul."

Alexiel spoke from the shadows, her voice a detached, analytical whisper. "He will have your head regardless, Magister. Your network is compromised. Your only remaining variable is whether the truth dies with you, or if you entrust it to someone who might actually listen."

Her cold pragmatism seemed to drain the last of the fight from him. He slumped in his chair, his gaze fixing on Artorius, clinging to the Prince's honor as a drowning man clings to a splinter of wood.

"He will kill them all," Lucian whispered. "That is why I had to burn the book."

Artorius leaned forward. "Kill who, Magister?"

"The ones on the list," he said, gesturing with his chin toward the book in Alexiel's hands. "That is not a list of heretics. It is a medical ledger. A private census of every member of the Empyrean Bloodline showing advanced stages of the Affliction."

The Prince was stunned into silence.

"We are not trying to overthrow the Imperium," Lucian continued, his voice gaining a desperate strength as he spoke to Artorius. "We are trying to save it from itself! The Empyrean Affliction is worsening with every generation of prescribed inbreeding. The madness is accelerating. We... my patrons and I... have been searching for a cure, a way to purify the bloodline before it collapses entirely."

He looked at Artorius, his old eyes pleading. "Your father sees this illness as a weakness to be purged, not a disease to be cured. If he gets that book, he will not see a list of patients. He will see a list of political rivals and 'flawed' bloodlines to be eliminated, plunging the Imperium into a civil war that will destroy us all."

The confession hung in the air, terrible and absolute. Artorius looked at Alexiel, his face pale with horror. They had come looking for a simple conspiracy of heretics. Instead, they had found the secret, rotting heart of the Imperium itself, and a book that could either save it or burn it to the ground.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: Magister Lucian Kantos's office, The Great Archives, Aeterna.]

Artorius bound the old man's hands himself, his movements efficient but lacking any cruelty. He sat the trembling Magister back down in his own ornate chair. The Prince paced before the desk, his face a mask of anger and betrayal. Alexiel, meanwhile, said nothing. She stood by the hearth, calmly examining the leather-bound book she had rescued from the flames.

"You were a trusted servant of the Imperium for two centuries," Artorius began, his voice tight with righteous fury. "You were the keeper of our history, our truth. And all along, you have been engaged in treason. I will have answers, Magister. Who are the Revisionist Scholars? What is your purpose?"

Lucian Kantos, though terrified, seemed to draw strength from his conviction. He lifted his chin, his eyes defiant behind their thick lenses. "My only treason was to the lies that hold this empire together, my Prince! We seek only the truth that your father has spent a thousand years burying in this very library!"

"A truth you were willing to burn to protect?" Artorius countered, gesturing to the book in Alexiel's hands.

"Some truths are too dangerous for the likes of Lord Regent Raziel!" Lucian shot back.

Alexiel finally looked up from the book. "This is not a history, Magister," she said, her voice quiet and analytical, cutting through the emotional confrontation. The two men fell silent, turning to her. "The binding is too new. The leather is Tsuran, not Imperial. And it has a hidden clasp."

She ran a finger along the spine, finding a nearly invisible seam. With a faint click, a small section of the cover opened, revealing not pages, but a tightly-rolled, coded scroll.

"This is not a history book," Alexiel repeated, her Unseeing Eyes fixed on the terrified old man. "This is a ledger. A list of names."

The color drained from Lucian's face. He stared at her, seeing not the "flawed Null" or the "honorable defector," but a mind as sharp and ruthless as Raziel's own. She had laid his entire conspiracy bare.

He looked at Artorius, at his honest, conflicted face. He made his choice. "What," he rasped, his voice a dry whisper of surrender, "do you want to know?"

Artorius pushed the scroll across the desk. "Decode it. All of it."

Lucian explained the cipher. Alexiel, with her innate grasp of patterns, understood it almost instantly. As the old man spoke, she unrolled the scroll. "The list is in two parts," she murmured. "The Afflicted... and the Patrons."

Her finger traced down the first list. "Lord Vorlag of House Sanguis. Commander of the Third Legion. It notes... 'bouts of extreme paranoia and violent rage'." She continued, "Lady Mara of House Jannus..." The list was a terrifying catalog of the rot beneath the gilded surface of the Empyrean elite. Her finger stopped.

She looked up at Artorius, her expression softening with a flicker of genuine pity. She turned the scroll so he could see the name she was pointing to.

Prince Titus val Artorius. Symptoms: Uncontrolled rage, paranoia, delusion of enemies. Accelerated by emotional trauma.

Artorius recoiled as if he'd been struck. The blood drained from his face. His brother... his uncontrollable rage was not just grief. It was the disease. The family curse.

"Who?" Artorius finally managed to say, his voice a choked whisper. "Who are the patrons? Who knows about this?"

Alexiel turned to the second list. The names there were just as shocking. There were nobles from rival houses, terrified of Raziel's potential purges. There was a high-ranking trade minister from the Tsuran Dominion. And then there was the last name, the one that made Artorius feel as though the floor had fallen away beneath him.

"Praetor Cassius," Alexiel read softly. "Chief advisor to the Lord Regent."

Lucian Kantos nodded grimly. "Even my Lord Raziel's closest confidant sees the truth. He fears what the Regent will do if he ever believes the bloodline itself is failing. We are not heretics, Prince. We are physicians, trying to cure a disease before the patient dies."

They stood in the silent office, the weight of the secret settling upon them. They now held a ledger that could tear the Imperium apart.

Alexiel stood by the window of her suite, the coded ledger resting on the table behind her like a sleeping serpent. The city of Aeterna was a perfect grid of light and order below, but her mind was a storm of chaotic new data. Artorius, bless his honorable heart, had left her to "rest," believing the confrontation with Lucian was over.

For her, it had just begun.

Her mind, the cold, strategic instrument Lucifer had honed, began to lay out the pieces on the board.

Asset 1: The Ledger. A list of the weak—Empyreans succumbing to the Affliction, including the Prince's own brother, Titus. A list of the conspirators—patrons funding a secret cure, including a traitor, Cassius, at the Regent's right hand. This is a weapon of immense power. Blackmail. Leverage. A private army of the desperate.

Asset 2: Lucian Kantos and the Scholars. A network of the Imperium's best minds, already organized and dedicated to solving the single greatest threat to the Empyrean bloodline. They are currently loyal to me out of fear.

Threat 1: Raziel's Order. The Lord Regent has commanded me to hunt and purge the Scholars. To disobey is to reveal myself as an enemy. To obey is to destroy a priceless asset and commit myself to his brutal ideology.

Threat 2: The Affliction itself. Her thoughts turned inward. She recalled the fight at the waterfall, the surge of cold, thrilling joy she felt as she dismantled her former comrades. She had dismissed it as battle focus, but the ledger's descriptions of the Affliction—"uncontrolled rage," "paranoia," "delusion"—felt crude, incomplete. What if the madness wasn't just rage? What if, in its purest form, it was a state of perfect, predatory clarity? A joyous embrace of one's own power, stripped of all sentimental weakness?

The thought was terrifying. Is that what I am? Is my "Joyful Predator" nature the same disease that is driving Titus to furious outbursts? She considered her own status as a Null. Perhaps my inability to channel magic has been a shield, preventing that flicker of joy from becoming a wildfire of true madness. My greatest perceived flaw... may have been my only salvation.

She pushed the thought away. It was a variable for another time. The immediate problem was Raziel. He had given her a test with only one correct answer: his. She needed to find another.

Her mind presented the options with clinical accuracy.

Option A: Obey the Regent.

The Plan: I deliver Lucian and the true ledger to Raziel. I use my skills to hunt down every last one of the Revisionist Scholars and their patrons, as commanded.

Pros: I would fulfill my mission perfectly. It would earn me a measure of Raziel's trust and solidify my position as a useful, if dangerous, tool. It is the simplest path.

Cons: It is a moral horror. It would destroy any chance of a cure. It would alienate Artorius completely, losing me a valuable ally. And it would make me nothing more than Raziel's personal executioner. Assessment: Unacceptable. This path ends with my soul shorn away, leaving only the weapon.

[CHOICE_ID: ObeyRaziel_1]

Option B: Defy the Regent.

The Plan: I reveal the truth to Artorius. We use the ledger to rally the "honorable" but secret patrons to our side. We confront my father-in-law—no, not yet—we confront the Lord Regent, and attempt to force a reform.

Pros: The path of honor. It would win Artorius's unwavering, permanent loyalty.

Cons: It is strategic suicide. Raziel's power is absolute. He has known of this conspiracy for years; this is his "honeypot." To step into it willingly would be to hand him all of his enemies on a silver platter. He would crush us, and the Imperium would fall into a civil war it could not survive. Assessment: Catastrophic failure guaranteed.

[CHOICE_ID: DefyRaziel_2]

Option C: Architect a New Truth.

The Plan: A deception. A dangerous, multi-layered gambit worthy of my bloodline.

Step 1: I will publicly accept Raziel's mission, appearing as his loyal hunter.

Step 2: I will use the information in the ledger to identify a small, expendable, and truly seditious cell of low-level heretics unconnected to the main scholarly body. I will lead Raziel's Silent Guard on a flawless, public purge of this "cancer," giving him the victory he wants.

Step 3: Simultaneously, I will take control of Lucian Kantos and the real Revisionist Scholars. I will move their research to a new, hidden location under my secret protection, funded by their own patrons, who I will now control through blackmail. I will allow them to continue their work on a cure, turning them from a liability into my own secret asset.

Pros: This satisfies Raziel's immediate demand, preserves the only hope for a cure, and gives me an immense network of secrets and influence.

Cons: It is incredibly risky. It requires deceiving Raziel, Artorius, and the entire Imperium. If any part of it fails, I will be exposed and annihilated. Assessment: High risk, high reward. The only path that leads to a desirable outcome.

[CHOICE_ID: DeceiveRaziel_3]

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: Magister Lucian Kantos's office, The Great Archives, Aeterna.]

A heavy, horrified silence filled the Magister's office. Artorius stared at the ledger, his face pale, the names of his brother and his father's most trusted advisor seeming to burn on the page. Lucian Kantos looked like a man awaiting his own execution. Only Alexiel remained calm, her expression analytical as she processed the immense strategic implications of the secret they now held.

"My brother..." Artorius finally whispered, shaking his head in disbelief. "All these noble houses... My father would see them all purged. He would call it 'cutting away the rot.' This is a catastrophe."

"Despair is a strategic error, my Prince," Alexiel said, her quiet voice cutting through his turmoil. All traces of the weary defector were gone, replaced by the focused authority of a commander. "This is not a catastrophe. It is an opportunity."

Both men looked at her, stunned.

She stepped forward, her gaze moving from the ledger to Artorius, and then to Lucian. "We cannot obey the Lord Regent's order. To kill these scholars would be to destroy the only hope of a cure. We also cannot defy him openly; he would crush us all without a second thought."

She began to pace slowly, her mind assembling a new plan from the ashes of the old one. "Therefore, we must present him with a new calculation. One where his desired outcome and our own align."

She stopped and looked at Artorius, her Unseeing Eyes seeming to see right through him. "You and I, with the Magister's full cooperation, will gather detailed evidence. Not just this ledger, but historical precedents from the archives, medical analyses of the Affliction's progression, and a projection of what will happen to the Empyrean bloodline if nothing is done."

Her plan was audacious, a gamble played for the highest possible stakes. "We will then go to your father not with heresy, but with a solution. We will not ask for mercy; we will present a strategic imperative."

She laid out the core of her argument, the words she would put in Artorius's mouth. "We will tell him the disease is real, and we cannot simply bury our heads in the sand. We will propose that he allow the scholars to continue their work—in absolute secret, under our direct supervision. We will not be defying his order to purge a heresy; we will be recruiting a medical team to mitigate a genetic threat to the long-term stability of the Imperium."

Lucian Kantos stared at her, a flicker of desperate, disbelieving hope in his ancient eyes. He had spent his life hiding in shadows, and this woman was proposing to turn his secret work into a sanctioned, if hidden, Imperial project.

Artorius was equally stunned, but for a different reason. He saw the sheer, brilliant audacity of her plan. It was a path that allowed him to protect the innocent, to potentially save his own brother, and to appeal to his father's cold pragmatism all at once. It was a move he never would have conceived of.

"It is a dangerous path," he said, his mind reeling.

"The only safe path," Alexiel replied, her voice soft but absolute, "is the one you control."

A new, secret alliance had just been forged between the Prince, the Traitor, and the Heretic.

ch 10

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Tarsakh, Day 11. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: Magister Lucian Kantos's office, The Great Archives, Aeterna.]
