Her plan was simple, desperate, and required absolute trust. Working in a terrifying, self-imposed silence, they followed her whispered commands. They dragged the heavy tables and benches, barricading all but one of the main doorways, creating a single, dark chokepoint. Then, they took the oil from every lamp they could find, pouring it carefully across the stone floor in a wide, glistening circle in the center of the room.

The trap was set. Now for the bait.

She looked at the younger of the two soldiers. "Marius," she said softly. "I need you to stand in the center of that circle. Look afraid. You are the last survivor, alone and terrified. Can you do that for me?"

The young man stared at her, his eyes wide with fear, but then he looked at the other, older soldier, who gave him a single, grim nod. He swallowed hard and walked to the center of the oil slick, his sword held in a shaking hand.

Alexiel and the other legionary melted into the deep shadows near the hearth. Alexiel held a single, lit torch, its flame cupped in her hand to hide its light.

They waited. The silence stretched, thick and suffocating. The only sound was Marius's ragged, intentionally loud breathing.

The skittering began again. But it was not from above. It was from the walls around them. A dry, scraping sound that seemed to come from all directions at once. The creature was inside the stone, moving, observing, hunting.

Suddenly, the air directly behind Marius began to shimmer.

With a silent warp of reality, the Chitinous Weaver materialized, its multifaceted eyes locked on its prey. It stood perfectly still for a moment, its obsidian-like limbs planted squarely in the center of the oil-slicked floor.

Marius cried out, a genuine scream of absolute terror.

From the shadows, Alexiel moved. This was the moment.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 14. Night.]

[Location: The Barracks Common Room, Seraph's Watch.]

[Physical exhaustion weighing on her movements]
The Weaver materialized behind the terrified soldier, Marius, its multifaceted eyes gleaming with cold, predatory intelligence. It uncoiled, ready for a silent, instant kill.

Marius’s scream was the signal.

From the shadows near the hearth, Alexiel moved. She didn't draw her sword. She threw the torch. It sailed through the air in a perfect, fiery arc and landed squarely in the center of the oil-slicked floor.

The world erupted in a deafening WHOOSH.

The oil ignited instantly, creating a raging wall of fire that engulfed the creature. For the first time, the silent predator made a sound. It was a high-pitched, piercing shriek of pure, unadulterated agony, a sound of scraping glass and tearing metal that grated on the soul. Its shimmering, phasing ability seemed to short-circuit in the intense heat; it was now a physical, trapped, and burning beast.

"Now!" Alexiel commanded, her voice cutting through the roar of the flames. "Keep it in the fire! Do not let it out!"

Her two soldiers, their fear momentarily burned away by the adrenaline of the successful ambush, surged forward. They kicked over heavy oak tables, creating a crude barricade around the inferno, using their longspears to jab at the creature, forcing it back into the heart of the flames whenever it tried to scramble out.

The burning Weaver was a vision of horror. Its obsidian carapace began to crack and glow with orange fissures. Enraged and in agony, it lunged through the flames, ignoring the spears. It was focused on the one who had lured it into the trap: Marius.

The young soldier, frozen in terror, was too slow to react. The creature’s burning forelimb lashed out, catching him across the chest. His armor sizzled as the burning, corrosive ichor of the creature ate through it. He collapsed with a single, final sigh.

"Back!" Alexiel shouted to the remaining veteran. As the creature turned its attention to them, Alexiel unleashed a final, desperate burst of her hidden power. A focused telekinetic blow, invisible in the fiery chaos, struck the creature's already-damaged head like a battering ram.

The Weaver shuddered, its shriek cutting off abruptly. It took one more stumbling step before collapsing into a charred, twitching ruin in the center of the dying flames.

Silence fell over the smoke-filled room, broken only by the crackle of the last embers. Alexiel and the lone surviving soldier stood panting, their faces grimy with soot. They had won. One was dead.

Alexiel looked at the smoldering corpse, her mind already analyzing its weaknesses, its reaction to fire, its final, desperate lunge. Then she looked at the body of young Marius. The victory felt hollow, the cost already too high.

And they both knew there were still two more of those things out there.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 14. Late Night.]

[Location: The Barracks, Seraph's Watch.]

[Physical exhaustion weighing on her movements]
In the smoky ruin of the common room, the surviving legionary, a grizzled veteran named Darius, looked at Alexiel, his eyes filled with a battle-hardened awe. "What now, my Lady? We hunt the others?"

Alexiel shook her head, her mind coldly processing the new tactical reality. Mission objective: reconnaissance. Objective complete. Threat identified: Chitinous Weaver, pack hunter, phases through solid matter, vulnerable to fire. Current force non-viable for extermination. Further engagement is not strategic; it is attrition.

"No," she said, her voice firm. "The mission is complete. We have the intelligence we came for. To continue with a force of two would be an act of ego, not strategy. We are leaving."

Darius stared at her, shock warring with his ingrained discipline. For a commander to choose retreat over a "glorious" last stand was almost unheard of in the Imperial military. It was also the smartest order he had ever received.

"The main gate is too heavy for two men to unbar," he said, his mind catching up. "How do we get out?"

"We go out the way we first planned to come in," Alexiel stated. "The aqueducts."

They moved from the barracks like phantoms, back into the silent, moonlit courtyard. Every shadow seemed to hold a waiting predator. The silvery, metallic filaments they had seen earlier seemed to glisten with a new menace on the walls. They crept from cover to cover, their destination a small, unassuming cistern building at the far end of the courtyard.

They were almost there when a flicker of movement from the rooftops caught Alexiel's eye. On the parapet of the keep above them, one of the Weavers stood silhouetted against the moon, its multifaceted eyes locked directly onto them. It let out a piercing, high-pitched shriek that echoed across the silent fortress—a cry of discovery, a call to its sibling.

"Run!" Alexiel yelled.

They sprinted the last fifty yards, diving headfirst into the dark, narrow opening of the aqueduct tunnel just as the second Weaver blinked into existence where they had been standing.

Without hesitating, Alexiel spun around in the cramped tunnel, placed her hand on the stone archway of the entrance, and unleashed the last vestiges of her power. A focused telekinetic blast tore at the rocks above, causing a small but effective rockslide that sealed the tunnel entrance behind them with a deafening crash. It wouldn't hold the creatures for long, but it would buy them the time they needed.

They stumbled through the long, dark tunnel, emerging minutes later into the cool, clean air of the mountainside. Exhausted and battered, they looked up at the high ridge. A single lantern flashed in the darkness—Cato's signal.

They were safe. They had survived. Alexiel leaned against the cold rock, the cost of the intelligence they had gathered weighing heavily upon her. Three men dead. A fortress held by an alien predator. The mission was over, but the war for Seraph's Watch was just beginning.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 15. Pre-Dawn.]

[Location: The Starfall Guard's ridge encampment.]

A signal lantern from the rocks above guided them through the final, treacherous part of the climb. Alexiel, leaning heavily on the veteran soldier Brandt, stumbled into the hidden encampment. Veteran-Sergeant Cato rushed to meet them, his craggy face a mask of immense relief that quickly curdled into grim understanding as he saw there were only two of them.

"My Lady," he began, his voice a low rumble. "You're wounded."

"The mission was a success," Alexiel stated, cutting him off. Her voice was strained with fatigue, but her eyes were sharp and clear. "Gather the squad leaders. We have work to do."

Minutes later, they were huddled around a low, shielded lantern, a rough map of Seraph's Watch scratched into the dirt before them. The five officers listened in stunned silence as Alexiel gave her report.

"The enemy is not of the Host," she said, her voice precise and clinical. "It is a predator. A pack hunter. For now, we will call them Chitinous Weavers."

She described their impossible speed, their ability to phase through solid matter, and the horrifying way they drained their victims, leaving behind desiccated husks. She detailed the metallic, web-like traps and the gruesome cocoons used to dissolve armor and steel.

"They have turned the fortress into a nest," she concluded. "We are facing a species of apex predator, not a disorganized military force."

The faces of the officers were pale in the lantern light. This was a foe from a nightmare, something no Imperial doctrine had ever prepared them for.

Alexiel did not let the fear fester. She immediately pivoted to strategy. "But now that we know what they are, we know their weaknesses."

She picked up a charred stick and drew on the map. "They are ambushers. They are silent. But they are not gods. We saw one burn." A grim smile touched her lips. "And it screamed. Fire disrupts their phasing ability and causes them extreme pain. We will use this."

She laid out the new plan. "We will not enter the aqueducts again. That way is compromised. We will assault the main gate."

Cato looked at her in disbelief. "A frontal assault?"

"A feint," Alexiel corrected. "We will use the gnomish alchemical charges we brought to create a breach, but not at the gate—at the wall of the main supply depot here," she tapped the map. "The explosion and subsequent fire will be our diversion. It will draw the creatures to the blaze."

"While they are distracted," she continued, "the true assault team—myself and a small squad—will go over the main wall here, under the cover of the chaos. The rest of you, led by Cato, will provide covering fire and eliminate any of the creatures drawn to the initial breach. Our mission is no longer reconnaissance. It is extermination. We will find their nest and kill them all."

The plan was incredibly dangerous, a multi-front, chaotic assault on a fortified position held by monsters. But it was proactive, it was based on sound intelligence she had risked her life to get, and it was delivered with an unshakable confidence that left no room for doubt.

The assembled officers looked at each other, then at their commander. They were soldiers of the newly-christened Starfall Guard. And they had their orders.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 15. Dead of Night.]

[Location: The valley outside Seraph's Watch.]

The fortress was a black monolith against a sky of cold, distant stars. The valley was utterly silent, the night air still. Two soldiers from the Starfall Guard, moving like shadows, crept to the base of the fortress’s large, squat supply depot. They carried a heavy, clay pot between them, filled with a viscous gnomish alchemical compound. With practiced, silent efficiency, they packed the charge against a key structural point in the wall, set a small, magically-timed detonator, and melted back into the darkness.

High above on the ridges, Cato watched through his spyglass, his heart hammering against his ribs. His forty best archers lay prone around him, their bowstrings taut, their arrows already tipped with pitch and oil.

At the base of the main fortress wall, a hundred yards from the supply depot, Alexiel and her five chosen soldiers crouched in the darkness. They held grappling hooks, their eyes fixed on the top of the rampart. She gave a final, sharp nod to her team. They were ready.

The world held its breath.

There was no loud noise. Just a deep, resonant thrum that seemed to vibrate in the very stone of the mountains. A network of sickly green cracks instantly spread across the supply depot's wall. Then, with a sound like a giant's sigh, the stone did not explode; it dissolved, crumbling into a massive cloud of dust and a wide, gaping breach.

"Archers!" Cato's voice was a low growl. "Now!"

A hundred flaming arrows soared through the night sky in a perfect, fiery arc, plunging down into the breach. They found dry grain, barrels of oil, and wooden stores. A second later, a raging inferno erupted within the fortress walls, casting a hellish, dancing light against the stone keep.

"Go," Alexiel commanded.

Her team sprang into action. Grappling hooks flew, biting into the stone of the main wall. Under the cover of the roaring fire and the sudden chaos, they began their swift, silent ascent.

Alexiel was the first over the top. She landed in a silent crouch on the battlements, her sword already in hand. Below her, the courtyard was beginning to fill with the sound she had been waiting for: the high-pitched, furious shrieks of the Chitinous Weavers, drawn from their lairs by the fire and the sudden intrusion.

The hunt had been reversed. Her team had now become the hunters, and they had just entered the nest.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 15. Dead of Night.]

[Location: Inside the walls of Seraph's Watch.]

[Physical exhaustion weighing on her movements]
Alexiel landed silently on the stone walkway of the rampart, her five chosen soldiers following a moment later. Below them, the fortress was a tapestry of chaos and fire. The inferno at the supply depot cast long, dancing shadows across the main courtyard, and the air was filled with the high-pitched, furious shrieks of the Chitinous Weavers as they were drawn to the blaze.

"The fire has them distracted," Alexiel whispered, her voice barely audible over the distant roar. "They believe the threat is there. That makes us the hunters. We move for the central keep. That is where the nest will be."

Each soldier nodded, their faces grim in the flickering firelight. They now carried lit torches in their off-hands, the flames a small but defiant ward against the phasing horrors they now faced.

They descended from the walls into the silent streets of the fortress proper, moving as one cohesive unit. Alexiel led them through a maze of narrow alleyways and covered archways, deliberately avoiding the open spaces. She was forcing the enemy to fight on her terms, in tight corridors where its ability to flank was neutralized.

As they passed the mess hall, a flicker of warped air coalesced on the wall beside them. A Weaver materialized, its multifaceted eyes glowing. Before it could strike, the five soldiers had already formed a tight, outward-facing circle, their torches creating a ring of protective fire. The creature hissed, the sound like grinding glass, and recoiled from the light and heat, unwilling to charge into the flames.

"It fears fire more than it desires a direct confrontation," Alexiel noted, her voice a clinical assessment. With a flick of her wrist, she unleashed a small burst of her secret magic—not a fireball, but a focused telekinetic blow that sent a nearby burning brazier tumbling towards the creature.

The Weaver shrieked as embers and fire washed over it, its phasing ability flickering erratically. Enraged and in pain, it made a reckless charge.

This time, the Starfall Guard was ready. They met its charge not with fear, but with disciplined fury. One soldier's shield took the brunt of the impact while two others thrust their spears into the weak points of its joints. Alexiel herself darted in, her sword a blur, and delivered the killing blow. The creature collapsed, silent once more.

As its life faded, a low, resonant hum seemed to echo from its chitinous shell, a sound that pulled faintly towards the massive, dark structure of the central keep.

"It was retreating," Alexiel realized aloud. "Trying to get back to the nest."

She followed the faint, pulling sensation, leading her small team through the silent dread of the fortress until they stood before a set of immense, iron-banded doors leading down into the foundations of the keep. The doors were coated in the thick, silvery, metallic webbing they had seen before, and from behind them came a faint, rhythmic, chittering sound. The sound of a thousand tiny things, all moving in unison.

They had found it.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 15. Night.]

[Location: The Catacomb Entrance, Keep of Seraph's Watch.]

[Physical exhaustion weighing on her movements]
There was no time for a complex plan. The rhythmic chittering from beyond the web-caked doors was growing louder, more agitated. The creatures knew they were here.

"The bar is on the other side," the veteran soldier, Brandt, grunted. "We'll have to force it."

"Then force it," Alexiel commanded.

Brandt and the other soldier slammed their armored shoulders against the heavy iron doors. The wood groaned in protest but held fast. Again, they charged, the sound echoing like a hammer blow in the silent fortress. On the third impact, the rotten bar on the other side finally splintered, and the doors burst inward.

They stumbled into a vast, cavernous space beneath the keep. The air was thick with a sickly sweet, metallic odor. The walls, floor, and ceiling were coated in the shimmering, silvery webbing, which pulsed with a faint, internal light. Dozens of desiccated Imperial soldiers were cocooned to the walls, their faces frozen in expressions of silent terror.

In the center of the cavern, a nightmarish form resided. It was a Chitinous Weaver, but one twice the size of the others, its carapace thicker, more ornate, like the grim throne of a monstrous queen. It was connected by thick, pulsating strands of webbing to the ceiling, where dozens of large, leathery egg-sacs hung like grotesque chandeliers. At its feet stood the other two Weavers, acting as its royal guard.

This was the nest. They had found the Broodmother.

As one, the three creatures turned their multifaceted eyes upon the intruders. The Broodmother let out a silent, psychic shriek that slammed into their minds, a wave of pure terror and alien hunger. The two soldiers cried out, stumbling back, their hands flying to their heads.

Alexiel, her mind fortified by a lifetime of discipline, fought through the psychic assault. The two smaller Weavers, their movements a blur, blinked across the room to attack her stunned men.

"The Queen!" Alexiel yelled, her voice cutting through the mental static. "She controls them! Ignore the guards, target the Queen!"

She knew a direct fight was unwinnable. She had to break the Broodmother's concentration. It was a desperate gambit. She used her burst of speed, channeling the last of her energy and her will into a single, decisive act of her secret magic.

She thrust her hand forward, and a lance of pure, white-hot concussive force—not a spell of fire, but of raw, focused power—erupted from her palm. It shot across the cavern and slammed directly into the massive Broodmother.

The creature shrieked, a sound both audible and psychic, a deafening wave of pure agony. Its connection to its guards faltered. The two smaller Weavers, who had been about to deliver killing blows to Alexiel's soldiers, froze for a split second, disoriented and confused.

In that same instant, the great iron doors behind them burst open again. It was Cato, leading the charge of the forty surviving members of the Starfall Guard, their torches and drawn swords flooding the cavern with light and the promise of battle.

They had arrived at the exact moment the tide was turning. The final battle for Seraph's Watch was about to begin.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 15. Night.]

[Location: The Nest, Catacombs of Seraph's Watch.]

[Physical exhaustion weighing on her movements]
The cavern doors burst open, and the disciplined ranks of the Starfall Guard flooded in, their torches creating a moving wall of defiant light. For a moment, the soldiers froze, their professionalism faltering at the sheer horror of the web-coated cavern and the screeching monstrosities within.

Alexiel’s voice cut through the chaos, sharp and absolute. "Cato! Shield walls, left and right! Pin the lesser drones against the walls! Archers, flaming arrows! Burn the webbing! Burn the nests! Smoke them out!"

Her commands were the steel spine her soldiers needed. Cato roared his affirmation, and the Guard moved with renewed purpose. Two shield walls advanced, using their torches to drive the two smaller Weavers back, pinning them against the sticky, metallic webbing. The creatures shrieked as the archers loosed volleys of flaming arrows into the egg-sacs on the ceiling, filling the cavern with thick, acrid smoke and the sickening pop of incinerating eggs.

The two smaller Weavers, enraged and blinded by the smoke and fire, were systematically dispatched by the disciplined soldiers, but not without cost. Several legionaries were caught by desperate, phasing lunges, their lives drained in an instant before their comrades could avenge them.

With its children burning and its guards dead, the wounded Broodmother finally detached itself from the wall. It was a creature of immense size and terrifying power, and it let out a psychic shriek of pure, focused rage that sent a wave of fear through the legion. It fixed its many eyes on the architect of its destruction: Alexiel.

"Hold the perimeter!" Alexiel commanded her troops. "This one is mine."

She knew a mob of soldiers would be useless against its phasing ability; it would blink into their midst and cause a massacre. It needed to be locked into a duel.

She advanced alone into the center of the cavern, her sword held ready. The Broodmother charged, not with a physical run, but with a series of short, disorienting blinks that made it almost impossible to track. But Alexiel wasn't tracking its position; she was anticipating its destination.

She met its first lunge with a perfect parry, her blade deflecting a serrated limb that would have torn through plate steel. She used her secret magic, a subtle telekinetic push, to slow one of its legs for a fraction of a second, causing the beast to stumble. To her soldiers watching from the perimeter, it looked like a feat of impossible martial timing.

The duel was a blur of motion—Alexiel’s dark steel against the creature's obsidian chitin. She was a prodigy, but the Broodmother was an ancient and powerful predator. It was faster and stronger. In a chaotic exchange, one of its limbs lashed out, catching her across the ribs with bone-crushing force. She cried out in pain, a fresh wave of agony joining the dull throb in her side. She was wounded, badly, but she was not broken.

The pain only sharpened her focus. She saw her opening. The Broodmother, seeing her falter, rose up to deliver the final, draining bite. It was the same arrogant over-commitment Ghor'mar had made.

With the last of her strength, Alexiel used her burst of speed. She didn't dodge. She charged forward, under its raised limbs, and plunged her sword with all her might into the soft, unprotected tissue beneath the creature's head, where it joined the main carapace.

The Broodmother went rigid. Its psychic shriek tore through the cavern one last time before it collapsed, a mountain of twitching, dying chitin.

Silence fell. Alexiel stood over the corpse, breathing heavily, her armor cracked and her body screaming in protest. Cato and the surviving soldiers stared in reverent awe.

"Report," she gasped.

Cato's face was grim. "Seventeen dead, my Lady. The cost was high."

Alexiel looked at the faces of her exhausted, bloodied soldiers. They had won. She had won. But as she looked at the carnage, the thrill of her 'Joyful Predator' nature was entirely absent, replaced only by the cold, heavy price of command.

ch 14 - retcon

Sleeper stuff

"My Lady, we can't go down there," Brandt said, his voice strained. "We don't know what else is..."

"Which is precisely why we must," Alexiel countered, her voice soft but absolute. "The mission is to identify the threat. We know what it is. Now we find out where it came from."

She took a torch and, without waiting for a reply, led the two veteran soldiers into the fissure. It was not a natural cave. The walls were smooth, worked stone, covered in faded glyphs of a language so ancient none of them could read it. They were in a place far older than the Imperium itself.

The tunnel opened into a vast, silent chamber. In the center lay a colossal, shattered object that looked like a stone egg, its pieces scattered across the floor. This was clearly the Broodmother's origin point. But scattered around it were other bodies—not Imperial soldiers, but skeletons clad in strange, form-fitting armor, their helmets bearing a sigil none of them recognized: a single, sleepless eye.

Alexiel knelt by one of the ancient corpses. Clutched in its skeletal hand was a thin, metallic data-slate, miraculously preserved. She picked it up. The script was a precursor to modern Imperial, but her mind, a prodigy's mind, could decipher the fragments.

...Year of the Sundering... driven them deep... the prison must hold... the Watch must be maintained...

The truth settled over her with the weight of a collapsing mountain. Seraph's Watch had not been built to guard the border against other mortal nations.

It had been built to be the lid on a cage. And the thing inside was waking up.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 16. Morning.]

[Location: An ancient chamber beneath Seraph's Watch.]

The three of them stood in the silent, ancient chamber, the dust of forgotten millennia thick in the air. The truth of the place settled upon them, a weight heavier than the mountain above. This was not a fortress. It was a prison. And the inmates were stirring.

"My Lady," Cato whispered, his veteran's composure finally cracking, his gaze fixed on the shattered stone egg. "What is this place?"

Alexiel looked from the ancient data-slate in her hand to the dark, unexplored tunnels leading deeper into the earth. A part of her, the relentless analyst, burned with the desire to know more, to push forward, to solve the ultimate mystery of what the Seraphim had buried here.

But the commander in her overrode that desire. Mission: Reconnaissance. Objective: Identify the threat. She looked at Cato and Brandt, at their exhausted faces, and thought of her battered soldiers on the ridge. Current force: forty-seven, fatigued. Enemy: Unknown number of apex predators with phasing abilities. Location: Inside their prison.

Further exploration is not strategy, she concluded with absolute conviction. It is ego. The mission is complete. The new mission is to ensure this intelligence reaches Aeterna.

She carefully secured the ancient data-slate in a pouch at her belt. "This place," she said, her voice quiet but absolute, "is a tomb we were not meant to open." She turned to her two companions. "Our work here is done. We are leaving. Now."

Their journey back through the fortress was a masterclass in controlled terror. Every shadow seemed to writhe, every silent hall felt as though it were watching them. They moved with a speed and stealth born of pure dread, expecting a shimmering horror to materialize at any moment. But nothing did. The fortress remained unnervingly still, as if the remaining creatures knew their secret had been discovered and were content to let them go, to let them carry their terrifying message back to the mortal world.

They emerged from the main gate into the bright morning sun, blinking like creatures born in darkness. They met the rest of the Starfall Guard, who had already begun breaking down their hidden camp.

Alexiel addressed her assembled, weary company. She did not tell them the full truth—the knowledge was too dangerous.

"The enemy within is not of the Host," she announced, her voice carrying across the ranks. "It is something older. Something the fortress was built to contain. Our mission is complete. We carry a message of vital importance to the Lord Regent."

She swung herself onto her horse, ignoring the protest of her still-healing wounds.

"We ride for Aeterna," she commanded, her voice ringing with a new, grim urgency. "With all possible haste."

The Starfall Guard, a small, battered company carrying a secret that could change the world, turned their backs on the silent prison of Seraph's Watch and began their long, urgent journey home.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 19. Night.]

[Location: A Starfall Guard encampment, The Eastern March.]

The camp was an island of disciplined quiet in the vast, dark wilderness. The thirty surviving members of the mission moved with a weary efficiency, their faces grim but their actions sharp. They were no longer the disgraced Third Regiment or a collection of Fortress Vigil veterans; they were a single, cohesive unit, forged into something new by the horrors of Seraph's Watch.

Alexiel sat by the low-burning fire, staring into the flames. The physical wounds on her side and shoulder had been sealed by the clerics' magic, leaving only a deep, profound ache. The fatigue, however, was a heavier burden, a weight on her very soul.

Veteran-Sergeant Cato approached, his heavy footsteps soft on the packed earth. He offered her a waterskin without a word. She took it and drank, the cool water a small comfort.

"You have not slept, my Lady," he said, his voice a low rumble. It was a statement of fact, not an accusation.

"My mind... processes the data," she replied, her gaze still fixed on the fire. "The original garrison were not soldiers. They were jailors. The Imperium has been guarding a prison for millennia and has forgotten what's inside."

Cato nodded grimly. "The men whisper of it. They don't understand what those things were, but they understand we faced something no legion has seen in a thousand years." He paused. "They also whisper your name."

Alexiel said nothing.

"Not 'The Sword of the Host'," Cato clarified. "Not 'The Traitor'. Just... 'The Commander'. It is a thing of respect. Of awe."

She finally looked up from the fire, her Unseeing Eyes meeting his in the flickering light. For a moment, the mask of the unshakable commander fell away, and he saw the profound exhaustion of the sixteen-year-old girl beneath it.

"I led seventeen of our men to their deaths, Cato," she said, her voice barely a whisper.

The old Orc's expression did not change, but his voice was filled with an absolute, unshakeable conviction. "No, my Lady," he corrected her firmly. "You led fifty of us into a tomb that should have claimed us all. You led thirty-three of us back out into the light."

He looked her square in the eyes. "That is not failure. That is a miracle. And it is a miracle they will follow to the end of the world."

A quiet understanding passed between them. It was not warmth or affection, but a bond of profound, shared experience and mutual respect forged in a nightmare.

Alexiel gave him a single, small nod of acknowledgement. The mask slid back into place. "See to the morning watch, Sergeant," she said, her voice once again that of a commander. "We break camp at first light."

Cato gave a crisp salute. "Yes, my Lady."

He left her to her thoughts, his loyalty to the strange, brilliant, and weary young woman now as solid and unbreakable as the mountains around them.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 22. Mid-day.]

[Location: A forested road in the Eastern March.]

They were less than a day's ride from the established Imperial border when Alexiel held up a single, sharp fist, calling the weary column to a halt. The forest around them had gone too quiet. The normal chatter of birds and insects had ceased.

A moment later, a dozen sleek, black-fletched arrows thudded into the trees around them, a silent, deadly warning. They were not crude Host arrows, but masterwork shafts fired with disciplined precision. The Starfall Guard reacted instantly, their training taking over. They formed a defensive circle, shields up, swords drawn, their eyes scanning the dense woods.

From the shadows emerged a group of warriors. They wore lacquered black armor, their faces hidden behind menacing, iron masks crafted to look like Oni demons. They carried long, curved blades and moved with a silent, fluid grace. They were outnumbered by the Starfall Guard, but they held the superior tactical ground.

Their leader, his helmet distinguished by a simple silver crescent, stepped forward. He removed his mask, revealing the sharp, intelligent face of a man in his prime. He spoke perfect, if slightly accented, Imperial.

"You are Imperial soldiers, far east of your designated patrol routes," he said, his voice calm and professional. He gestured to their battered armor. "You have seen battle. We have noted the silence from Seraph's Watch. We request an explanation."

Cato moved to Alexiel's side. "Tsuran Dominion patrol," he growled. "They have no authority here."

Alexiel dismounted, handing her reins to Brandt. She walked forward alone, holding up a hand to show she was unarmed. "I am Princess Alexiel of the Imperium, Commander of this company," she announced, her voice clear and strong. "We are on a sanctioned mission by order of the Lord Regent."

The Tsuran Captain's eyes widened slightly at her title, a flicker of surprise at her youth. "A Princess? So far from the capital? An interesting development. I am Captain Kenji of the Tsuran Dominion. My orders are to ascertain the reason for the fortress's silence."

"Your orders are fulfilled," Alexiel replied smoothly, meeting his gaze. "Seraph's Watch was attacked by a rogue Host warband. We have eliminated the threat."

Captain Kenji remained unconvinced. "A Host warband capable of taking a fortress like the Watch is unheard of. We would need to verify your claim. My men and I will accompany you back to the fortress."

He was testing her, probing for weakness. Alexiel did not flinch. "That will be impossible," she said, her tone shifting from diplomatic to authoritative. "The Host employed unclean beasts. The area is now under Imperial quarantine due to extreme biological hazard. To allow your men inside would be to risk a plague crossing the border. For the safety of your own people, Captain, you must remain clear of Seraph's Watch. That is a decree from the Imperium."

She had turned his request into a matter of his own people's safety, giving him an honorable reason to back down.

Captain Kenji studied her for a long, tense moment. He knew he was being stonewalled by a girl half his age, but her logic was sound, and her authority was absolute. He gave a sharp, formal bow.

"Very well, Princess. The Dominion will respect your quarantine. For now." His eyes narrowed slightly. "But know that we will be watching. The silence of Seraph's Watch is a matter of great concern to us."

With a silent hand signal, Captain Kenji and his patrol melted back into the forest as silently as they had appeared. The standoff was over. Alexiel had won, not with a blade, but with a perfectly constructed lie. But now she knew—another great power was watching, and her secret was becoming harder to keep.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Mirtul, Day 4. Night.]

[Location: Starfall Guard Encampment, Aeterna Provincial Road.]

Fatigue: 0

The Starfall Guard's camp was a model of the disciplined efficiency Alexiel had drilled into them. It was their final night on the road; by noon tomorrow, they would see the walls of Aeterna.

Inside her command tent, Alexiel sat cross-legged before a low table. The two artifacts from Seraph's Watch lay before her: the ancient, metallic data-slate and the smooth, teardrop-shaped obsidian crystal recovered from the Broodmother. The rest of the camp slept, but her mind was alight. She knew that what she presented to Raziel tomorrow could change the course of the Imperium, and she needed every possible advantage.

She focused first on the data-slate, running her fingers over the strange, archaic glyphs. The language was a precursor to modern Imperial, its syntax almost unrecognizable, but the roots were there. She closed her eyes, channeling a small, secret trickle of her magical energy, not into a spell, but into her own mind, sharpening her focus, allowing her to see the connections and patterns in the ancient grammar.

Fragments of meaning began to surface from the damaged text.

...the Weavers are not the prisoners. They are the wardens... their purpose is to maintain the great seal...

...their song silences the deep dreams... the Sleeper Below must not be woken...

...we have failed. The Watch is broken. The silence is the key...

Alexiel's blood ran cold. Not prisoners... wardens. The creatures they fought were the guardians of the prison, not its inmates. The true threat, the "Sleeper Below," was something else entirely. Seraph's Watch wasn't a cage for the Weavers; it was a lock on the door to something far, far worse.

She pushed the slate aside, her gaze falling on the obsidian crystal. It hummed with a faint, latent energy. It had been the creature's core, its focus. Perhaps it held an answer.

Hesitantly, she picked it up. She focused her will, pushing a tiny thread of her own energy into the stone.

Her mind exploded in a chaos of alien senses. For a terrifying second, she saw the world through the Broodmother's multifaceted eyes—the cavern not as a dark tomb, but a warm, vibrant nest. She felt a fierce, possessive love for the glowing egg-sacs, and a deep, instinctual, primal terror of the deep, silent presence sleeping in the rock beneath her.

The psychic feedback was overwhelming. Alexiel cried out and dropped the stone, stumbling back, a thin trickle of blood running from her nose. She gasped for air, the human world slowly swimming back into focus.

She now understood. The report she had to deliver to Raziel tomorrow was no longer just a military assessment of a new hostile species. It was a warning of an ancient, apocalyptic threat that the Imperium had forgotten ever existed, and whose jailors were now dead.

ch 14

### Scene 1: Aftermath in the Nest
[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 15. Late Night.]

[Location: The Broodmother's Nest, Seraph's Watch.]

The cavern was filled with the acrid stench of burnt chitin and scorched webbing. The surviving members of the Starfall Guard were tending to their wounded, their movements slow with exhaustion and shock. The adrenaline had faded, leaving only the grim reality of their losses.

Alexiel, however, was already moving. Ignoring the searing pain in her ribs, she approached the colossal, smoldering corpse of the Broodmother.

"Cato," she called out, her voice sharp and clear. "Brandt. Get me samples."

The two veteran soldiers looked at her, their faces etched with confusion. "My Lady?" Cato asked.

"This creature is an unknown variable," Alexiel explained, her tone that of a lecturer. "To defeat it elsewhere, we must understand it. The Glimmering Combine would pay a fortune for these materials. The Lord Regent would pay even more for the strategic advantage." She pointed with her blade. "I want carapace fragments and a vial of the corrosive fluid. We are not looting; we are securing a priceless asset."

Her cold, pragmatic logic was undeniable. Reluctantly, the soldiers began the grisly work.

While they worked, Alexiel conducted her own investigation. She confirmed that the cocoons were used for breaking down materials, finding the half-dissolved remains of Imperial soldiers and their wargear inside. This was not a simple predator; it was a harvester.

"My Lady, look at this," Brandt called out from the corpse of the Broodmother.

Alexiel came to his side. He pointed into the creature's cracked-open head. Near its primary nerve cluster, nestled in a bed of strange, crystalline fibers, was a smooth, tear-drop shaped stone of polished obsidian. With the creature's death, it was now pulsing with a faint, slow, internal light.

As Alexiel reached in and her fingers closed around the stone, a profound and shocking sensation washed over her. It was silence. For a split second, the constant, low-level thrum of ambient magic that had been a background noise to her entire life was utterly gone.

It nullifies, she realized with a jolt. It erases magic.

She quickly concealed the crystal in a secure pouch, her mind reeling with the implications. She looked at Cato as he approached. "What is it, my Lady?"

"A command node, I believe," she lied smoothly, her voice betraying nothing. "For controlling the hive. The Imperial Magi will find it interesting."

She had just acquired the secret to an ultimate weapon, and her first instinct was to hide it from everyone.

### Scene 2: A Commander's Worth
[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 16. Pre-Dawn.]

[Location: The Broodmother's Nest, Seraph's Watch.]

The cavern was no longer a nest; it was a tomb, and now, a fortress. The surviving members of the Starfall Guard, summoned from the ridge by Cato, had secured the entrance. Veteran-Sergeant Cato sat on a crate near a low fire, methodically cleaning his sword. Across from him, Brandt stared into the flames, his hands still trembling slightly.

"I've fought for twenty years, Cato," Brandt said, his voice a hoarse whisper. "I've never seen anything like that thing. The way it just... appeared." He shook his head. "Or the way she fought it."

Cato grunted, not looking up from his whetstone. "She knew," he said, his voice a low rumble. "While we were seeing a monster, she was seeing a machine. She found its gears, and she broke them."

"But the cost," Brandt said, looking at the cots where their wounded comrades lay. "So many dead."

"Aye," Cato agreed. "The cost was high. But under any other commander? We would all be husks right now. They would have formed a shield wall in the valley and been slaughtered."

He gestured with his chin towards the far side of the cavern. Alexiel was not resting. She knelt on the stone floor, her wounds freshly dressed. By the light of a single lantern, she had the obsidian crystal and was sketching its intricate, faint patterns into a journal, her focus absolute. She was not a commander mourning her dead; she was a scholar dissecting a specimen.

"She is not like us," Cato grunted softly, a statement of fact. "She bled with us. She walked into the trap with us. But her mind... it does not feel victory or defeat. It only solves the problem in front of it."

Brandt watched her for a long moment, his terror slowly being replaced by the unwavering faith of a man who has survived a nightmare because his commander looked into the heart of it and did not flinch.

### Scene 3: The Last Report
[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 16. Morning.]

[Location: The Keep, Seraph's Watch.]

The next morning, a healed Alexiel led a small team on a final, thorough search of the fortress. In the slain fortress commander's chambers, amidst desiccated corpses, they found his personal logbook, miraculously preserved.

Alexiel read the final entries aloud to Cato and Brandt. The commander described the initial appearance of a few creatures from a deep, previously unknown fissure in the fortress foundations. He wrote of their terrifying ability to phase through walls and kill his men in their sleep. His last entry was a desperate, scrawled testament.

"The garrison is gone. I have barred myself in my chambers, but the scraping at the door has stopped. It is silent now. I think... I think it knows it can get in whenever it wants. It is toying with me. If anyone finds this... do not try to reclaim this fortress. Burn it to the ground. Burn the whole damned valley."

Alexiel closed the book. The truth was simpler and grimmer than any ancient prison. There was no "Sleeper Below." Seraph's Watch had simply fallen to a superior, invasive species that had burrowed up from the deep earth.

She looked at her men. "Our mission was to identify the threat. We have. This knowledge, and what we have recovered from the creatures, is too vital to risk. We are retreating to report our findings."

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 20. Night.]

[Location: A hidden camp in the foothills of the Eastern March.]

Fatigue: 0

The camp was quiet, the surviving members of the Starfall Guard lost in an exhausted, well-earned sleep. Only the sentries walked the perimeter, their dark forms outlined against the starry sky. Inside her small command tent, Alexiel was not sleeping.

By the light of a single, flickering candle, she held the obsidian teardrop she had taken from the Broodmother. It was cool and smooth in her palm, absorbing the candlelight and giving nothing back. She remembered the sensation when she had first touched it in the nest: a profound, shocking silence in the magical world.

She had to know more. This was not a variable she could leave unknown.

She placed the candle on a small, flat rock in the center of her tent. Its flame was a living thing, a tiny, dancing beacon of warmth and simple fire magic. This would be her test.

Closing her eyes, Alexiel held the crystal in both hands and focused. She recalled that feeling of absolute nullity. She pushed a tiny, controlled thread of her own energy—her secret, innate magic—into the stone.

The effect was instantaneous. The crystal grew ice-cold in her hands. The air in the tent became heavy, dead. The cheerful, dancing flame of the candle did not go out; it changed. It froze in place, losing its flicker, its radiant heat diminishing until it was just a static, sad, perfectly still teardrop of light. It was as if the very concept of fire had forgotten what it was supposed to do.

Her mind, a prodigy's mind, analyzed the phenomenon with awe. It doesn't destroy magic. It suppresses it. It imposes a state of absolute, mundane reality. A state of... Null.

The name for her own public condition, her greatest lie, suddenly had a new and terrifying meaning.

She pushed a little more energy into the crystal. The field of silence expanded. The candle flame was snuffed out completely, not with a puff of smoke, but as if it had simply ceased to exist. The minor enchantments woven into her own armor felt dull and inert. A low, humming pressure began to build inside her skull. She realized with perfect clarity that controlling this power required immense discipline. It was not like casting a spell; it was like holding back the ocean with nothing but your will.

She severed the flow of energy.

With a gasp, the world rushed back in. The ambient hum of magic returned. The pressure in her head vanished, leaving her feeling drained but utterly, terrifyingly exhilarated.

She looked down at the smooth, black stone in her hands. She finally understood the truth that had been hidden from her entire life. She was not a "flawed" Null, incapable of magic. Her very nature, her deepest secret, was the mastery of the Null state itself.

She carefully wrapped the crystal in cloth and hid it deep within her pack. She now possessed the ultimate weapon in a world ruled by magic-wielding celestials. A secret that could bring the entire Imperium to its knees.

We will now return to the scene with the Tsuran patrol, rewriting it to reflect Alexiel's new canonical status as a veteran warrior commander and the hardened, veteran nature of her surviving Starfall Guard.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Eleint, Day 22. Mid-day.]

[Location: A forested road in the Eastern March.]

The thirty-three surviving members of the Starfall Guard moved through the dense forest with the grim efficiency of true veterans. They were no longer a disgraced regiment; they were a hardened, elite company who had been forged in the nightmare of Seraph's Watch. Their march was quiet, their eyes constantly scanning the trees.

Alexiel, at their head, held up a single, sharp fist, and the entire column froze as one. The woods had gone too quiet.

A moment later, a dozen sleek, black-fletched arrows thudded into the trees around them, a silent, deadly warning. Instantly, the Starfall Guard formed a disciplined, outward-facing shield wall, their movements economical and sure.

From the shadows emerged a group of warriors in black, lacquered armor, their faces hidden behind iron masks. Tsuran. Their leader, his helmet distinguished by a silver crescent, stepped forward, removing his mask.

"You are Imperial soldiers, far east of your designated patrol routes," he said, his voice calm, but his eyes widened slightly as he took in the state of their armor and the formidable discipline of their formation. "You have seen heavy battle. We have noted the silence from Seraph's Watch. We require an explanation."

Alexiel dismounted and stepped forward, her presence radiating an authority that belied her sixteen years. "I am Princess Alexiel, Commander of the Starfall Guard," she stated, her voice clear and carrying. "We are on a sanctioned mission by order of the Lord Regent."

The Tsuran Captain, Kenji, gave a respectful but wary bow. "A Princess-Commander. The rumors did not do you justice. My orders are to ascertain the reason for the fortress's silence."

"Then your orders are fulfilled, Captain," Alexiel replied smoothly. "Seraph's Watch was destroyed. We were ambushed by a Host splinter faction wielding profane beasts and heretical alchemy we had not seen before. We eliminated the warlord and his abominations, but the cost was high."

It was a masterful lie, wrapped around a core of truth.

Captain Kenji remained skeptical, but he was also a professional. He was facing a legendary commander leading a veteran force that was clearly capable of immense violence. "Unclean beasts? Heretical alchemy? We would need to verify such a claim. My patrol will accompany you."

Alexiel’s gaze hardened slightly. "That will be impossible," she said, her tone shifting from diplomatic to absolute. "The site is now under Imperial quarantine by order of the Lord Regent, pending an investigation by our Magi. The alchemical residue is highly volatile. For the safety of your own men, you must remain clear of Seraph's Watch."

She had given him a threat disguised as a concern, and an order wrapped in a justification of safety.

Captain Kenji studied her for a long, tense moment. He was outmatched, and she had given him an honorable reason to withdraw without losing face. He gave a sharp, formal bow.

"Very well, Princess. The Dominion will respect your quarantine. For now." His eyes narrowed. "But be assured, we will be watching."

With a silent hand signal, Captain Kenji and his patrol melted back into the forest. The standoff was over. Alexiel had faced her first political test since the battle and had won, securing her apocalyptic secret for a little while longer.

Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 78. Month of Mirtul, Day 5. Afternoon.] [Location: The Chamber of Stilled Stars, Empyrean Citadel, Aeterna.]

They stood before Raziel in the cold, silent heart of his power. Artorius, as the Prince, began the report. "Father, Commander Alexiel has returned from Seraph's Watch. The mission was a success, but the fortress is lost. Her findings are... disturbing." He stepped back, ceding the floor.

All of Raziel's attention, a force as palpable and heavy as gravity, settled on Alexiel.

She stepped forward, her face a calm, professional mask. She laid out the events with clinical precision: the silent fortress, the discovery of the desiccated garrison, the battle with the phasing predators she had named Chitinous Weavers, and the final, costly assault on the nest that had annihilated the Broodmother.

"We recovered the personal logbook of the fortress's last commander," Alexiel continued, placing the battered book on the stone floor between them. "And this... from a deeper, more ancient chamber beneath the nest." She produced the metallic data-slate.

"The slate tells us the history of the fortress itself," she said, her voice clear and steady. "It was the final report of a First Surveyor team from the dawn of the Imperium. Seraph's Watch was not built to guard the border, Lord Regent. It was built to contain the creatures within that valley. It is a prison, and we have just killed its wardens."

Raziel’s Starlit Eyes narrowed, a flicker of something unreadable in their cosmic depths. He had just learned of a threat that had been hidden from even him for millennia.

Alexiel placed the final pieces of evidence on the floor: sealed containers holding fragments of chitin and vials of the corrosive fluid her soldiers had gathered. "The Broodmother itself seemed to be the nexus of the hive's intelligence. Its destruction caused the lesser creatures to fall into disarray. We have secured these biological samples for the Imperial Magi to study."

She said nothing of the smooth, obsidian crystal. It remained hidden, its faint, silent hum a secret known only to her, resting in a secure pouch at her belt.

Raziel was silent for a very long time, his ancient mind processing this new, apocalyptic variable. "The Tsuran must not learn the truth of this," he whispered finally. "The border must be sealed permanently. This... species... represents an existential threat."

He looked at Alexiel, his assessment of her now complete. She was not a Trojan Horse. She was a being who had survived a forgotten nightmare and returned with its secrets. She was, for the moment, invaluable.

"You are the world's sole expert on this enemy," Raziel commanded. "You will form and lead a new, special commission, under my direct authority. You will have access to the Imperial Magi, the Great Archives, whatever you need. You will analyze these materials, and you will devise a comprehensive strategy to contain or eradicate this threat."

He had given her an impossible task, and with it, an unprecedented level of power and authority. Artorius watched, proud but also wary. The woman he was to marry was becoming a power unto herself, and she was now armed with a secret he couldn't possibly imagine.

ch 15 - timeskip

### The Three-Year Time Skip: The Rise of the Magister
Starting Point: Alexiel is veteran warrior (Tier 3). She has been promoted to Magister of the Watch and is newly married to Prince Artorius. The world is tense after the events at Fortress Vigil and Seraph's Watch.

### Year One: The Foundation
Alexiel's Focus: Establishing her authority, beginning her secret research, and solidifying her power base both politically and militarily.

Month 1-2: Alexiel establishes the "Seraph's Watch Commission" in a secure wing of the Magi's tower in Aeterna, which she names "The Eyrie." She uses her authority to hand-pick a team of the Imperium's most brilliant (and discreet) alchemists, engineers, and scholars, shocking them by proving to be their intellectual superior in every meeting.

Month 3: In the deep privacy of her warded labs, she conducts her first successful experiment with the Broodmother's crystal, creating a small, stable Nullification Field. The act is mentally draining but proves her theory correct: the power can be controlled.

Month 4-6: The Starfall Guard is permanently garrisoned in Aeterna under her direct command. She subjects them to relentless training, integrating her anti-Weaver tactics and Host-style guerilla warfare principles into their Imperial discipline. Their reputation as an unorthodox and terrifyingly effective unit grows.

Month 7-8: Her political life solidifies. She navigates the treacherous court with Artorius as her shield, flawlessly maintaining her facade. She is seen by the nobility as a quiet, dutiful wife who happens to have a strange and bloody hobby.

Month 9: Covert Mission. Alexiel leads a small, elite team of her most trusted Starfall Guard back to the sealed Seraph's Watch. Their high-risk mission is a success: they capture several live, smaller Weaver specimens for study, a feat no one believed possible.

Month 10-12: She begins to wean herself off the crystal, meditating on the "feeling" of the Nullification effect and attempting to replicate it with her own innate, secret magic. It is an immense struggle of will and concentration.

The Conspirators' Plot: Matriarch Tiberia and Prince Titus make their first secret contact with the Glimmering Combine in Nexus, commissioning a "device to soothe an afflicted mind" under the false pretext of helping a distant, unstable relative.

Other Factions: The Unchained Host, under Lucifer's command, regroups after the defeat at Fortress Vigil and begins a campaign of political subterfuge and probing raids along the border. The Tsuran Dominion quietly builds up its military presence on the border near Seraph's Watch, using the Imperium's new "quarantine" as an excuse.

### Year Two: The Weaver Purge & The Heirs
Alexiel's Focus: Applying her research to solve the Weaver problem permanently, while securing her place in the Imperial dynasty.

Month 1-8: The Weaver Purge. Armed with a deep understanding of the creatures' biology from the live specimens, Alexiel's commission develops new weapons: alchemical agents that dissolve Weaver webbing and specialized carapace-piercing arrowheads. She then spends the better part of the year leading her Starfall Guard in a brutal, systematic extermination campaign throughout the valley and upper catacombs of Seraph's Watch. The campaign is a stunning success, but it is costly, resulting in the deaths of twenty members of the Starfall Guard. The sacrifice cements the unit's legendary status and their fanatical devotion to the commander who bled with them.

Month 9: The twin sons, Cassian and Darius, are born. The birth of healthy, male heirs to Artorius solidifies Alexiel's position within the Empyrean Bloodline, to the disgust of the hardliners.

Month 10-12: With the birth of her children, Alexiel begins to adopt her "God-Warrior" mask in her private life. She loves her sons fiercely, but her inability to be truly vulnerable forces her to express it through lessons of strength and discipline, not simple affection, a change that a loving but concerned Artorius begins to notice.

The Conspirators' Plot: The Glimmering Combine delivers a prototype "Psychic Damper" to Tiberia's agent for an exorbitant price. It is unstable and heretical. They begin cautious, secret tests on low-value prisoners.

Other Factions: Artorius, now a proud father and seeing Alexiel as the proven savior of the Western March, becomes her greatest political champion in the Senate, using his influence to secure any resources her commission demands.

### Year Three: The Ascendant
Alexiel's Focus: Cementing her absolute power and shifting her long-term focus from the Weavers to the greater threat: Lucifer.

Month 1-3: Alexiel, through intense mental discipline, fully masters the Nullification Field. She can now create and sustain it without the crystal, though doing so is still mentally taxing. Her true power has reached its current zenith.

Month 4-5: Her daughter, Sariel, is born. Her family is now complete. Her relationship with Artorius has settled into a powerful and effective political partnership, though an emotionally distant marriage.

Month 6-8: The Starfall Guard, equipped with new Weaver-carapace armor prototypes developed by her commission, are now unquestionably the most elite fighting force in the Imperium.

Month 9: Alexiel presents her final report on the "Weaver Threat" to Raziel and the Senate. She declares the species "functionally extinct" and presents a stunning array of new military technologies derived from her research. She has solved the problem she was given and, in doing so, has made herself indispensable.

Month 10-12: With her official mission complete, she uses her immense new influence to pivot the Imperium's focus. She argues that the Weaver threat proves the Imperium is vulnerable to "unconventional threats," a clear and deliberate reference to Lucifer's Host. She begins retraining the Starfall Guard with a new, singular purpose: to be the ultimate weapon in the war against her father.

The Result: The time skip ends. Alexiel is a celebrated and feared High Commander. To the public, she is a veteran warrior Null who has achieved impossible feats through sheer will. Her secret, effective Level is 18 (Tier 3), making her a true peer of the remaining Apostates.

The Conspirators' Plot: Tiberia and Titus believe their Psychic Damper is now stable enough to use. They are ready to make their move to "cure" Titus and turn Artorius against his wife. The stage is set for the next great conflict.

ch 16

The time skip is executed. Three years have passed.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 81. Month of Ches, Day 10. Afternoon.]

[Location: The Prince's Suite, Zenith Spire, Aeterna.]

Fatigue: 0

Feats: Alert, War Caster, Mage Slayer (Assumed)

Three years had transformed Alexiel. The uncertain defector was gone, replaced by the Magister of the Watch, a celebrated hero of the Imperium and a figure of immense power. The Starfall Guard was now her personal legion, the most elite fighting force in the empire, armed with strange new weapons and armor derived from her secret research.

She stood watching her sons. Cassian and Darius, now energetic toddlers, sparred on a plush carpet with blunted wooden swords. She observed their movements with the cool, analytical eye of a commander assessing recruits, not the warm gaze of a mother. This was the "God-Warrior" mask she had forged for her family: a persona of distant, perfect strength.

Artorius entered the room, a weary but fond smile on his face. The years had deepened the lines of responsibility around his eyes. "Cassian has your fire," he said, coming to stand beside her. "Darius has your focus."

"Fire without focus is a weakness," Alexiel replied without looking away from the boys. "Focus without fire is a liability. They must learn to temper both."

Her assessment was, as always, tactical. Artorius sighed softly, his hope for a simpler warmth from his wife a long-faded memory. Theirs was a partnership of immense respect and efficiency, but an emotionally spartan one.

A servant entered then, bowing low and presenting a scroll sealed with the crest of Prince Titus. Artorius took it, his expression clouding with concern. He broke the seal and read. As he did, his face transformed, the weary lines replaced by a look of stunned, burgeoning hope.

"By the Creator," he whispered. He looked at Alexiel, his eyes shining with an emotion she had learned to see as a dangerous vulnerability. "It's from Titus. He... he requests an audience. With both of us."

He read from the scroll, his voice thick with hope. "'My dearest brother, I have... undergone a profound change... and wish to reconcile our house and heal the wounds of the past...'"

Artorius looked up, his heart laid bare. "He wants to make peace, Alexiel."

Alexiel’s mind, however, saw not an olive branch, but the glint of a hidden dagger. A profound change? Titus is a creature of pure, unrestrained rage, fueled by the Affliction. Such natures do not simply change.

"We will meet with him, of course," she said, her voice calm and supportive, a perfect echo of a dutiful wife.

But her mind was already calculating. This was not the move of a madman. It was the move of a chess piece, positioned by a player she could not yet see.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 81. Month of Ches, Day 15. Evening.]

[Location: A Grand Salon, Villa Varrick, Aeterna.]

The salon of Matriarch Tiberia Varrick was the heart of the political web in Aeterna. Tonight, it was a glittering affair, a gathering of nobles ostensibly for a poetry recital, but truly for the far more serious business of exchanging alliances and veiled threats. Cressida moved through the crowd with an easy, practiced grace, her smile warm, her eyes sharp. Her new position as companion to the controversial Princess Alexiel made her both an object of intense curiosity and a pariah, a status she wielded like a shield and a key.

Her target was not the Matriarch herself, but a much softer link in the chain: Lord Decian of House Nero, a vain and ambitious young noble known to be in Tiberia's inner circle. Cressida spotted him by the wine fountain, preening and holding court with a group of lesser lords.

She created a "chance" encounter, moving past his group and allowing her silken sleeve to brush his arm. "My pardon, Lord Decian," she said, her voice a perfect blend of apology and charm. She gave his tunic an appreciative glance. "That is stunning embroidery. The golden thread of the southern provinces, is it not? You have a remarkable eye for quality."

Decian, puffed up by the attention from the infamous princess's confidante, beamed. "Lady Cressida. You are too kind. One must maintain standards, after all."

"Indeed," Cressida said, taking a goblet of wine from a passing servant. She leaned in slightly, her voice becoming more conspiratorial. "And no one maintains a higher standard than your patron, Matriarch Tiberia. She seems... revitalized these past months. So full of purpose."

"The Matriarch is a pillar of the Imperium," Decian declared proudly.

"Oh, of course," Cressida agreed. "Her dedication to the royal house is inspiring, especially with the Prince Titus's miraculous recovery. It is wonderful to see him so... calm." She sighed, a masterful performance of wistful admiration. "One wonders how she manages it all. Such devotion requires access to resources far beyond my own small house."

Decian, eager to display his importance and insider knowledge, took the bait completely. He leaned closer. "The Matriarch understands that to solve a delicate Imperial problem," he whispered, "one must sometimes seek solutions from outside the Imperium. Her new contacts in the Glimmering Combine's Nexus branch have proven most... effective."

The confirmation hit Cressida like a physical blow, but her charming smile never wavered. Nexus. The Combine. So that's her vector.

"How very resourceful of her," Cressida said, her eyes wide with feigned admiration. "A true lesson in statecraft." She gave him a conspiratorial wink. "Thank you for the lovely conversation, my Lord. You have been most illuminating."

She turned and gracefully melted back into the crowd before he could realize he had just given away the conspiracy's greatest secret. Her smile remained in place, a perfect mask hiding the mind of a predator who had just found the scent of her prey.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 81. Month of Ches, Day 12. Afternoon.]

[Location: Prince Titus's Suite, Zenith Spire, Aeterna.]

The doors to Prince Titus's suite were opened by a servant whose face was a mixture of relief and disbelief. Artorius entered with a hopeful stride, Alexiel a step behind him, her expression a careful mask of neutral courtesy.

Titus stood waiting for them in the center of the room. The change was profound and deeply unsettling. The furious flush was gone from his face, replaced by a calm, thoughtful pallor. The restless, violent energy that had always surrounded him was gone, replaced by an aura of serene self-control. He looked at them, and for the first time, there was no rage in his eyes.

"Brother," he said, his voice measured and calm. "Lady Alexiel. Thank you for coming."

Artorius was so stunned by the change he was momentarily speechless. "Titus...?"

Titus gave a small, sad smile. "The fever has passed, Artorius. I have spent months in meditation, coming to terms with my... affliction. And the dishonor I have brought upon our house." He turned to Alexiel, his bow deep and formal. "My Lady," he said, his voice resonating with a sincerity that seemed flawless. "My grief over our mother's death made me a monster. I directed my pain at you, who had suffered the most. My words at your wedding were unforgivable. I can only beg for your pardon."

Artorius’s face was alight with pure joy. This was the moment he had prayed for. He rushed forward and embraced his brother. "There is nothing to forgive, Titus! To have you back, to have you well..."

Alexiel watched the reunion, her mind a cold, silent engine of analysis. The transformation is too perfect. The apology is too well-rehearsed. The Empyrean Affliction is a genetic decay; it does not simply vanish. This is not healing. This is suppression. Someone is controlling him.

She inclined her head gracefully. "You were in pain, my Prince," she said, her voice a perfect echo of compassionate understanding. "The Imperium is made stronger by your recovery."

Titus smiled, a calm, rational expression that was more terrifying than any of his old rages. "Thank you, my Lady." He turned back to Artorius. "Brother, might I have a word with you? Alone? For the sake of our family."

Artorius, his heart soaring with hope, readily agreed. "

Alexiel gave a small nod and retreated to the antechamber, her expression one of polite deference. The moment the door closed, her face became a mask of cold concentration.

Inside, Titus placed a hand on his brother's shoulder. "Artorius," he began, his voice now laced with a new, serious urgency. "My... illness... it gave me much time to think. I see things more clearly now. The threats to our house." He looked his brother in the eyes. "I was wrong to attack your wife with rage. My methods were flawed. But my fear, brother... my fear was not misplaced."

He began to speak, his words calm and logical, weaving a devastating tapestry of concern. He spoke of Alexiel's control over the military's most elite unit, of her secret research, of her unsettling influence. He twisted her every success into a sign of a secret, growing ambition that could one day threaten them all.

Artorius listened, his own joy and relief making him vulnerable. He heard not a conspirator, but his long-lost brother, finally speaking with reason and concern for their family.

The seed of doubt, expertly planted, began to take root.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 81. Month of Ches, Day 12. Late Afternoon.]

[Location: The Prince's Suite, Zenith Spire, Aeterna.]

When Artorius returned from his private talk with Titus, the soaring hope had vanished from his face. He was quiet, his expression clouded and thoughtful. Alexiel, who had been waiting patiently in the antechamber, saw the change instantly. The poison has been administered, she thought, her mind going on high alert while her face remained a mask of polite concern.

They walked back to their main suite in silence. Artorius paced to the window, staring down at the city, his back to her.

"Titus is... changed," he said finally, his voice heavy. "He seems clear-headed for the first time in years. We spoke at length." He paused, struggling with the words. "He... raised some concerns."

Alexiel remained silent, allowing him to wrestle with his thoughts.

"He worries about your position," Artorius continued, turning to face her. "About the influence you now command with the Starfall Guard. He fears that your power has grown outside the traditional structures, that it could become a destabilizing force." He was careful to frame it as his brother's fear, not his own, but the seed of doubt was there in his eyes.

Alexiel listened, her expression shifting to one of profound, sorrowful understanding. This was the attack. And she would not meet it with anger or denial. She would meet it with a truth so disarming it would leave him with no defense.

"He is right to be concerned, Artorius," she said softly.

The simple agreement stunned him into silence.

"I am a former enemy of the state," she continued, her voice quiet but firm. "I was raised by Lucifer himself. I command the most ruthlessly effective regiment in the capital. I hold secrets that could shatter this empire." She looked at him, her Unseeing Eyes holding a deep, convincing sadness. "From a purely strategic standpoint, I am the single greatest internal threat to your house. Your brother is not wrong to see it. Your father sees it as well."

She then allowed a flicker of her "Reluctant Champion" persona to show, the mask he had first fallen for. "Every day, I am terrified of that power. I never wanted it. I am a soldier, Artorius, not a politician. The Guard is loyal to me because I bled with them, not because I seek to lead a coup."

She took a small step towards him, her final move in this dangerous game. "But if my presence here, if my command, brings such discord to your house... if you believe I am a threat..." She held his gaze, her expression one of absolute, vulnerable sincerity. "Then tell me. I will step down. I will relinquish command of the Guard this very day. My loyalty is to the peace you are trying to build, and to you. I will place myself entirely at your discretion."

It was a perfect checkmate. She had validated his fears, demonstrated her strategic understanding, reaffirmed her own noble reluctance, and then handed him all the power. She knew his honor would never allow him to accept her resignation under such circumstances.

Artorius stared at her, any doubt he held now drowned in a wave of shame for his own suspicion. He saw not a schemer, but a hero, willing to sacrifice her own hard-won authority for the sake of his family's unity.

"No," he said, his voice thick with emotion as he closed the distance between them. "Never. I am sorry I even spoke of it. My brother is... still recovering. I will not let his fears poison what we are building together."

He took her hand, his trust in her now more absolute than ever. Alexiel allowed herself to return the gesture, her face a mask of quiet relief.

But internally, her mind was cold and clear. The attack did not come from the front. It came from the side, through him. They are more cunning than I thought. I must be more careful.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 81. Month of Ches, Day 13. Night.]

[Location: A secure safe house, Undercity of Aeterna.]

The room was spartan, a forgotten chamber deep in the foundations of the capital, far from the prying eyes of the Zenith Spire. Here, Alexiel met with her true inner circle. Ser Gideon Vance stood guard at the door, a silent monolith. Veteran-Sergeant Cato, his face grim, stood by the table. And at her side was Lady Cressida Valeriana, her sharp eyes missing nothing.

Alexiel unrolled a simple map of the Spire's noble quarters. "Titus's recovery is a fabrication," she stated, her voice cold and absolute. "The timing is too convenient. The change is too absolute. It is a performance, and Matriarch Tiberia is the director. They used him to plant a seed of doubt in Artorius. It was a successful attack."

Her companions listened, their expressions hardening.

"A direct counter-accusation is useless," Alexiel continued. "We have no proof, and Artorius's hope for his brother's recovery makes him vulnerable. We cannot attack their story. We must attack its foundation. We need to find the source of his 'cure'."

She looked at each of her allies, assigning their roles with quiet precision.

"Cressida," she began, turning to the young noblewoman. "You have the ear of the court. I need to know everything about Matriarch Tiberia's recent movements. Who has she met with? What off-world shipments has House Varrick received through Nexus? Who are her contacts with the Glimmering Combine?"

Cressida gave a sharp, predatory smile. "It will be my pleasure, my Lady."

Alexiel then turned to her most loyal soldier. "Cato. I need eyes on Titus's personal guard. Are any of them new? Do any of them carry strange devices? His 'cure' requires maintenance. Someone is getting close to him. I want to know who."

The old Orc nodded, his hand resting on the pommel of his axe.

Finally, she looked at Gideon. "You will remain my shadow. But through your barracks contacts, I need you to find me one of the apothecaries that serves House Varrick. I want to know what strange, non-traditional ingredients they have been ordering from off-world."

Her plan was set. A three-pronged investigation aimed at the heart of the conspiracy.

"While you are gathering intelligence," she concluded, "I will be in the Great Archives. If this 'cure' is technological or alchemical, there will be a record of its theory somewhere in a forbidden text. The answer is there. We will find it."

Her team looked at her, their expressions a mixture of awe and fierce loyalty. They were no longer just her protectors; they were her agents in a silent, secret war. Alexiel had been backed into a corner by the court's vipers, and she had responded by becoming a viper herself.

[Timestamp: Year of the Unchained Host, 81. Month of Ches, Day 15. Evening.]

[Location: A Grand Salon, Villa Varrick, Aeterna.]

The salon of Matriarch Tiberia Varrick was the heart of the political web in Aeterna. Tonight, it was a glittering affair, a gathering of nobles ostensibly for a poetry recital, but truly for the far more serious business of exchanging alliances and veiled threats. Cressida moved through the crowd with an easy, practiced grace, her smile warm, her eyes sharp. Her new position as companion to the controversial Princess Alexiel made her both an object of intense curiosity and a pariah, a status she wielded like a shield and a key.

Her target was not the Matriarch herself, but a much softer link in the chain: Lord Decian of House Nero, a vain and ambitious young noble known to be in Tiberia's inner circle. Cressida spotted him by the wine fountain, preening and holding court with a group of lesser lords.

She created a "chance" encounter, moving past his group and allowing her silken sleeve to brush his arm. "My pardon, Lord Decian," she said, her voice a perfect blend of apology and charm. She gave his tunic an appreciative glance. "That is stunning embroidery. The golden thread of the southern provinces, is it not? You have a remarkable eye for quality."

Decian, puffed up by the attention from the infamous princess's confidante, beamed. "Lady Cressida. You are too kind. One must maintain standards, after all."

"Indeed," Cressida said, taking a goblet of wine from a passing servant. She leaned in slightly, her voice becoming more conspiratorial. "And no one maintains a higher standard than your patron, Matriarch Tiberia. She seems... revitalized these past months. So full of purpose."

"The Matriarch is a pillar of the Imperium," Decian declared proudly.

"Oh, of course," Cressida agreed. "Her dedication to the royal house is inspiring, especially with the Prince Titus's miraculous recovery. It is wonderful to see him so... calm." She sighed, a masterful performance of wistful admiration. "One wonders how she manages it all. Such devotion requires access to resources far beyond my own small house."

Decian, eager to display his importance and insider knowledge, took the bait completely. He leaned closer. "The Matriarch understands that to solve a delicate Imperial problem," he whispered, "one must sometimes seek solutions from outside the Imperium.
